In a critical review, Wolf (2021) points out that these commonly promulgated anti-ageing compounds (resveratrol, rapamycin, nicotinamide mononucleotide and metformin) all cause weight loss, a feature that is "downplayed" in many anti-ageing publications; it is therefore likely that the compounds only counteract the life-shortening effects of obesity, and would not benefit individuals who have normal body weight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolf2021_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wolf2021-182">[182]</a></sup>
</p><p>Scientists have begun to explore calorie-restriction mimetics-natural and synthetic drug compounds that might yield the same health effects as calorie restriction, without dieting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> These investigations are still in their early stages. Evidence in both animals and humans suggests that <a href="/wiki/Resveratrol" title="Resveratrol">resveratrol</a> may be a caloric restriction mimetic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lam2013_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lam2013-184">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/Metformin" title="Metformin">metformin</a> was under study for its potential effect on slowing ageing in the worm <a href="/wiki/Caenorhabditis_elegans" title="Caenorhabditis elegans"><i>C.elegans</i></a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acheta_domesticus" title="Acheta domesticus">cricket</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pry2015_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pry2015-185">[185]</a></sup> Its effect on otherwise healthy humans is unknown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pry2015_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pry2015-185">[185]</a></sup> In 2019, Fahy and colleagues reported that a two-year trial on nine humans using metformin to regenerate thymus tissue unexpectedly resulted in a reversal of ageing as measured by DNA methylation levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fahy2019_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fahy2019-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sirolimus" title="Sirolimus">Rapamycin</a> was first shown to extend lifespan in eukaryotes in 2006 by Powers <i>et al.</i> who showed a dose-responsive effect of rapamycin on lifespan extension in yeast cells.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid16418483_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid16418483-187">[187]</a></sup> In a 2009 study, the lifespans of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mice" title="Mice">mice</a> fed rapamycin were increased between 28 and 38% from the beginning of treatment, or 9 to 14% in total increased maximum lifespan. Of particular note, the treatment began in mice aged 20 months, the equivalent of 60 human years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid19587680_188-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid19587680-188">[188]</a></sup> Rapamycin has subsequently been shown to extend mouse lifespan in several separate experiments,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Miller2010_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-Miller2010-189">[189]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ingram&amp;Roth2011_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ingram&amp;Roth2011-190">[190]</a></sup> and is now being tested for this purpose in nonhuman primates (the <a href="/wiki/Marmoset" title="Marmoset">marmoset</a> monkey).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tardif2015_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tardif2015-191">[191]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cancer geneticist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ronald_A._DePinho" title="Ronald A. DePinho">Ronald A. DePinho</a> and his colleagues published research on mice where <a href="/wiki/Telomerase" title="Telomerase">telomerase</a> activity was first genetically removed. Then, after the mice had prematurely aged, they restored telomerase activity by reactivating the telomerase gene. As a result, the mice were rejuvenated: Shrivelled testes grew back to normal and the animals regained their fertility. Other organs, such as the spleen, liver, intestines and brain, recuperated from their degenerated state. "[The finding] offers the possibility that normal human ageing could be slowed by reawakening the enzyme in cells where it has stopped working" says Ronald DePinho. However, activating telomerase in humans could potentially encourage the growth of tumours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup>
</p><p>Most known genetic interventions in <i>C. elegans</i> increase lifespan by 1.5 to 2.5-fold. As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the record for lifespan extension in C. <i>elegans</i> is a single-gene mutation which increases adult survival by tenfold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reis2009_67-2"><a href="#cite_note-Reis2009-67">[67]</a></sup> The strong conservation of some of the mechanisms of ageing discovered in model organisms imply that they may be useful in the enhancement of human survival. However, the benefits may not be proportional; longevity gains are typically greater in <i>C. elegans</i> than fruit flies, and greater in fruit flies than in mammals. One explanation for this is that mammals, being much longer-lived, already have many traits which promote lifespan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reis2009_67-3"><a href="#cite_note-Reis2009-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mitochondria-targeted antioxidant SkQ1 has been shown to extend the lifespan of mice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid22166671_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid22166671-193">[193]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_projects_and_prizes">Research projects and prizes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research projects and prizes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some research effort is directed to slow ageing and extend healthy lifespan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> 
In 1993, the Established populations for epidemiologic studies of the elderly,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> also known as the Yale Health and Aging Study, showed the importance of physical activity and argued against negative stereotypes concerning old age.
</p><p>Dr. David Snowdon's Nun Study on aging and Alzheimer's disease has many interesting discoveries about memory, the impact of positively expressed emotions and how to live a longer, higher quality life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup>
</p><p>A paper published on 29 March 2022 by a group of scientists at <a href="/wiki/Insilico_Medicine" title="Insilico Medicine">Insilico Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Chicago" title="University of Chicago">University of Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Mason_University" title="George Mason University">George Mason University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Liverpool" title="University of Liverpool">University of Liverpool</a> demonstrated that there might be several alternative senolytic targets and pathways that can be targeted with small molecules drugs. They use <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> models to yield a list of dual-purpose targets implicated in ageing and <a href="/wiki/Aging-associated_diseases" title="Aging-associated diseases">age-associated diseases</a>. It may impact multiple age-associated diseases and retard ageing for extending healthspan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup>
</p><p>The US <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_on_Aging" title="National Institute on Aging">National Institute on Aging</a> currently funds an intervention testing programme, whereby investigators nominate compounds (based on specific molecular ageing theories) to have evaluated with respect to their effects on lifespan and age-related biomarkers in outbred mice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> Previous age-related testing in mammals has proved largely irreproducible, because of small numbers of animals and lax mouse husbandry conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> The intervention testing programme aims to address this by conducting parallel experiments at three internationally recognised mouse ageing-centres, the <a href="/wiki/Barshop_Institute" title="Barshop Institute">Barshop Institute</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UTHSCSA" title="UTHSCSA">UTHSCSA</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a> at Ann Arbor and the <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Laboratory" title="Jackson Laboratory">Jackson Laboratory</a>.
</p><p>Several companies and organisations, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Calico" title="Google Calico">Google Calico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_Longevity" title="Human Longevity">Human Longevity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Venter" title="Craig Venter">Craig Venter</a>, Gero,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/SENS_Research_Foundation" title="SENS Research Foundation">SENS Research Foundation</a>, and Science for Life Extension in Russia,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> declared stopping or delaying ageing as their goal.
</p><p>Prizes for extending lifespan and slowing ageing in mammals exist. The <a href="/wiki/Methuselah_Foundation" title="Methuselah Foundation">Methuselah Foundation</a> offers the Mprize. Recently, the $1 Million Palo Alto Longevity Prize was launched. It is a research incentive prize to encourage teams from all over the world to compete in an all-out effort to "hack the code" that regulates our health and lifespan. It was founded by <a href="/wiki/Joon_Yun" title="Joon Yun">Joon Yun</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-palo_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-palo-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society_and_culture">Society and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Society and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aging_and_society" title="Aging and society">Aging and society</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Gerontology" title="Gerontology">Gerontology</a></div><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097025294">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right plainlinks sistersitebox">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-image"><img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Wiktionary-logo-en-v2.svg/40px-Wiktionary-logo-en-v2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Wiktionary-logo-en-v2.svg/60px-Wiktionary-logo-en-v2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Wiktionary-logo-en-v2.svg/80px-Wiktionary-logo-en-v2.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
<div class="side-box-text plainlist">Look up <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quadragenarian" title="wiktionary:quadragenarian">quadragenarian</a></b></i>, <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quinquagenarian" title="wiktionary:quinquagenarian">quinquagenarian</a></b></i>, <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sexagenarian" title="wiktionary:sexagenarian">sexagenarian</a></b></i>, <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/septuagenarian" title="wiktionary:septuagenarian">septuagenarian</a></b></i>, <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/octogenarian" title="wiktionary:octogenarian">octogenarian</a></b></i>, or <i><b><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/nonagenarian" title="wiktionary:nonagenarian">nonagenarian</a></b></i> in Wiktionary, the free dictionary.</div></div>
</div>
<p><span class="anchor" id="Dividing_the_lifespan"></span>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:003_p4_dd.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/003_p4_dd.JPG/220px-003_p4_dd.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/003_p4_dd.JPG/330px-003_p4_dd.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/003_p4_dd.JPG/440px-003_p4_dd.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:003_p4_dd.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An elderly man</div></div></div>
<p>Different cultures express age in different ways. The age of an adult human is commonly measured in whole years since the day of birth. Arbitrary divisions set to mark periods of life may include: <a href="/wiki/Minor_(law)" title="Minor (law)">juvenile</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Infant" title="Infant">infancy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Childhood" title="Childhood">childhood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Preadolescence" title="Preadolescence">preadolescence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adolescence" title="Adolescence">adolescence</a>), <a href="/wiki/Emerging_adulthood_and_early_adulthood" title="Emerging adulthood and early adulthood">early adulthood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_age" title="Middle age">middle adulthood</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senior_citizen" title="Senior citizen">late adulthood</a>. More casual terms may include "teenagers", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tween_(demographic)" title="Tween (demographic)">tweens</a>", "twentysomething", "thirtysomething", etc. as well as "denarian", "vicenarian", "tricenarian", "quadragenarian", etc.
</p><p>Most legal systems define a specific age for when an individual is allowed or obliged to do particular activities. These age specifications include <a href="/wiki/Voting_age" title="Voting age">voting age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legal_drinking_age" title="Legal drinking age">drinking age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Age_of_consent" title="Age of consent">age of consent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Age_of_majority" title="Age of majority">age of majority</a>, <a href="/wiki/Age_of_criminal_responsibility" title="Age of criminal responsibility">age of criminal responsibility</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marriageable_age" title="Marriageable age">marriageable age</a>, <a href="/wiki/Age_of_candidacy" title="Age of candidacy">age of candidacy</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mandatory_retirement_age" title="Mandatory retirement age">mandatory retirement age</a>. Admission to a movie for instance, may depend on age according to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_picture_rating_system" title="Motion picture rating system">motion picture rating system</a>. A bus fare might be discounted for the young or old. Each nation, government and non-governmental organisation has different ways of classifying age. In other words, <a href="/wiki/Chronology" title="Chronology">chronological</a> ageing may be distinguished from "social ageing" (cultural age-expectations of how people should act as they grow older) and "biological ageing" (an organism's physical state as it ages).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup>
</p><p>Ageism cost the United States $63 billion in one year according to a <a href="/wiki/Yale_School_of_Public_Health" title="Yale School of Public Health">Yale School of Public Health</a> study.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> In a UNFPA report about ageing in the 21st century, it highlighted the need to "Develop a new rights-based culture of ageing and a change of mindset and societal attitudes towards ageing and older persons, from welfare recipients to active, contributing members of society".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century-213">[213]</a></sup> UNFPA said that this "requires, among others, working towards the development of international human rights instruments and their translation into national laws and regulations and affirmative measures that challenge age discrimination and recognise older people as autonomous subjects".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century_213-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century-213">[213]</a></sup> Older people's music participation contributes to the maintenance of interpersonal relationships and promoting successful ageing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> At the same time, older persons can make contributions to society including caregiving and volunteering. For example, "A study of Bolivian migrants who [had] moved to Spain found that 69% left their children at home, usually with grandparents. In rural China, grandparents care for 38% of children aged under five whose parents have gone to work in cities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century_213-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics">Economics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Population_ageing" title="Population ageing">Population ageing</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2017_world_map,_median_age_by_country.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="864" decoding="async" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/2017_world_map%2C_median_age_by_country.svg/400px-2017_world_map%2C_median_age_by_country.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/2017_world_map%2C_median_age_by_country.svg/600px-2017_world_map%2C_median_age_by_country.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/2017_world_map%2C_median_age_by_country.svg/800px-2017_world_map%2C_median_age_by_country.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2017_world_map,_median_age_by_country.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing median age figures for 2017</div></div></div>
<p>Population ageing is the increase in the number and proportion of older people in society. Population ageing has three possible causes: migration, longer <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> (decreased death rate) and decreased birth rate. Ageing has a significant impact on society. Young people tend to have fewer legal privileges (if they are below the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_majority" title="Age of majority">age of majority</a>), they are more likely to push for political and social change, to develop and adopt new technologies, and to need education. Older people have different requirements from society and government, and frequently have differing values as well, such as for property and pension rights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vincent_2005_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vincent_2005-215">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 21st century, one of the most significant population trends is ageing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Currently, over 11% of the world's current population are people aged 60 and older and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Population_Fund" title="United Nations Population Fund">United Nations Population Fund</a> (UNFPA) estimates that by 2050 that number will rise to approximately 22%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century_213-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century-213">[213]</a></sup> Ageing has occurred due to development which has enabled better nutrition, sanitation, health care, education and economic well-being. Consequently, fertility rates have continued to decline and life expectancy has risen. Life expectancy at birth is over 80 now in 33 countries. Ageing is a "global phenomenon", that is occurring fastest in developing countries, including those with large youth populations, and poses social and economic challenges to the work which can be overcome with "the right set of policies to equip individuals, families and societies to address these challenges and to reap its benefits".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unfpa.org_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-unfpa.org-217">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>As life expectancy rises and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Birth_rates" title="Birth rates">birth rates</a> decline in developed countries, the <a href="/wiki/Median" title="Median">median</a> age rises accordingly. According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, this process is taking place in nearly every country in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-devrep05_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-devrep05-218">[218]</a></sup> A rising median age can have significant social and economic implications, as the workforce gets progressively older and the number of old workers and retirees grows relative to the number of young workers. Older people generally incur more health-related costs than do younger people in the workplace and can also cost more in worker's compensation and pension liabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aging-workforce_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-aging-workforce-219">[219]</a></sup> In most developed countries an older workforce is somewhat inevitable. In the United States for instance, the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Labor_Statistics" title="Bureau of Labor Statistics">Bureau of Labor Statistics</a> estimates that one in four American workers will be 55 or older by 2020.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aging-workforce_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-aging-workforce-219">[219]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (March 2022)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Among the most urgent concerns of older persons worldwide is income security. This poses challenges for governments with ageing populations to ensure investments in pension systems continues in order to provide economic independence and reduce poverty in old age. These challenges vary for developing and developed countries. UNFPA stated that, "Sustainability of these systems is of particular concern, particularly in developed countries, while social protection and old-age pension coverage remain a challenge for developing countries, where a large proportion of the labour force is found in the informal sector."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century_213-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>The global economic crisis has increased financial pressure to ensure economic security and access to health care in old age. In order to elevate this pressure "social protection floors must be implemented in order to guarantee income security and access to essential health and social services for all older persons and provide a safety net that contributes to the postponement of disability and prevention of impoverishment in old age".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century_213-5"><a href="#cite_note-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>It has been argued that population ageing has undermined economic development<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basakha_2015_220-0"><a href="#cite_note-Basakha_2015-220">[220]</a></sup> and can lead to lower inflation because elderly individuals care especially strongly about the value of their pensions and savings  Evidence suggests that pensions, while making a difference to the well-being of older persons, also benefit entire families especially in times of crisis when there may be a shortage or loss of employment within households. A study by the Australian Government in 2003 estimated that "women between the ages of 65 and 74 years contribute A$16 billion per year in unpaid caregiving and voluntary work. Similarly, men in the same age group contributed A$10 billion per year."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century_213-6"><a href="#cite_note-Ageing_in_the_Twenty-First_Century-213">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to increasing share of the elderly in the population, health care expenditures will continue to grow relative to the economy in coming decades. This has been considered as a negative phenomenon and effective strategies like labour productivity enhancement should be considered to deal with negative consequences of ageing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basakha_2014_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-Basakha_2014-221">[221]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sociology">Sociology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sociology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Menneske_Aldrene_(C._W._Eckersberg).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="931" data-file-width="1120" decoding="async" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Menneske_Aldrene_%28C._W._Eckersberg%29.png/220px-Menneske_Aldrene_%28C._W._Eckersberg%29.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Menneske_Aldrene_%28C._W._Eckersberg%29.png/330px-Menneske_Aldrene_%28C._W._Eckersberg%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Menneske_Aldrene_%28C._W._Eckersberg%29.png/440px-Menneske_Aldrene_%28C._W._Eckersberg%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Menneske_Aldrene_(C._W._Eckersberg).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Christoffer_Wilhelm_Eckersberg" title="Christoffer Wilhelm Eckersberg">Christoffer Wilhelm Eckersberg</a>: <i>Ages of Man</i></div></div></div>
<p>In the field of sociology and mental health, ageing is seen in five different views: ageing as <a href="/wiki/Maturity_(psychological)" title="Maturity (psychological)">maturity</a>, ageing as decline, ageing as a life-cycle event, ageing as generation, and ageing as survival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> Positive correlates with ageing often include economics, employment, marriage, children, education, and sense of control, as well as many others. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_science_of_aging" title="Social science of aging">social science of ageing</a> includes disengagement theory, activity theory, selectivity theory, and continuity theory. <a href="/wiki/Retirement" title="Retirement">Retirement</a>, a common transition faced by the elderly, may have both positive and negative consequences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> As cyborgs currently are on the rise<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> some theorists argue there is a need to develop new definitions of ageing and for instance a bio-techno-social definition of ageing has been suggested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid25456627_224-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid25456627-224">[224]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is a current debate as to whether or not the pursuit of <a href="/wiki/Longevity" title="Longevity">longevity</a> and the postponement of senescence are cost-effective health care goals given finite health care resources. Because of the accumulated infirmities of old age, bioethicist <a href="/wiki/Ezekiel_Emanuel" title="Ezekiel Emanuel">Ezekiel Emanuel</a>, opines that the pursuit of longevity via the <a href="/wiki/Compression_of_morbidity" title="Compression of morbidity">compression of morbidity</a> hypothesis is a "fantasy" and that human life is not worth living after age 75; longevity then should not be a goal of health care policy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Emmanuel_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-Emmanuel-225">[225]</a></sup> This opinion has been contested by neurosurgeon and medical ethicist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miguel_Faria" title="Miguel Faria">Miguel Faria</a>, who states that life can be worthwhile during old age, and that longevity should be pursued in association with the attainment of quality of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Faria_75_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-Faria_75-226">[226]</a></sup> Faria claims that postponement of senescence as well as happiness and wisdom can be attained in old age in a large proportion of those who lead healthy lifestyles and remain intellectually active.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Faria_longevity_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-Faria_longevity-227">[227]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care_demand">Health care demand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Health care demand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With age inevitable biological changes occur that increase the risk of illness and disability. UNFPA states that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unfpa.org_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-unfpa.org-217">[217]</a></sup>
</p><p>"A life-cycle approach to health care – one that starts early, continues through the reproductive years and lasts into old age – is essential for the physical and emotional well-being of older persons, and, indeed, all people. Public policies and programmes should additionally address the needs of older impoverished people who cannot afford health care."
</p><p>Many societies in Western Europe and Japan have ageing populations. While the effects on society are complex, there is a concern about the impact on health care demand. The large number of suggestions in the literature for specific interventions to cope with the expected increase in demand for long-term care in ageing societies can be organised under four headings: improve system performance; redesign service delivery; support informal caregivers; and shift demographic parameters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Saltman2006_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-Saltman2006-228">[228]</a></sup>
</p><p>However, the annual growth in national health spending is not mainly due to increasing demand from ageing populations, but rather has been driven by rising incomes, costly new medical technology, a shortage of health care workers and informational asymmetries between providers and patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rheinhardt2003_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rheinhardt2003-229">[229]</a></sup> A number of health problems become more prevalent as people get older. These include mental health problems as well as physical health problems, especially <a href="/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">dementia</a>.
</p><p>It has been estimated that population ageing only explains 0.2 percentage points of the annual growth rate in medical spending of 4.3% since 1970. In addition, certain reforms to the Medicare system in the United States decreased elderly spending on home health care by 12.5% per year between 1996 and 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Meara2004._230-0"><a href="#cite_note-Meara2004.-230">[230]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-perception">Self-perception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Self-perception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As humans age, their bodies begin to break down and their skin begins to look different, but people do not always welcome these changes to their appearance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beauty_standards" title="Beauty standards">Beauty standards</a> have evolved over time, and as scientific research in cosmeceuticals has increased, the industry has also expanded; the kinds of products they produce (such as serums and creams) have gradually gained popularity and become a part of many people's personal care routine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-232"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup> The cosmeceutical industry is currently the fastest growing beauty industry, with a market size of $49.5 billion for the year 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup>
</p><p>The increase in demand for cosmeceuticals has led scientists to find ingredients for these products in unorthodox places. For example, cryptomphalus aspersa secretion (or brown garden snail secretion) has been found to have antioxidant properties, increase skin cell proliferation, as well as increase extracellular proteins such as collagen and fibronectin (important proteins for cell proliferation).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup> Another substance used to prevent the physical manifestations of ageing is onobotulinumtoxinA, the toxin injected for Botox.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup>
</p><p>Generally, aversion to aging is a Western attitude. However, in other places around the world, old age is celebrated and honored. In Korea, for example, a special party called <a href="/wiki/Hwangap" title="Hwangap">hwangap</a> is held to celebrate and congratulate an individual for turning 60 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup> In China, respect for elderly is often the basis for how a community is organized and has been at the foundation of Chinese culture and morality for thousands of years. Older people are respected for their wisdom and most important decisions have traditionally not been made without consulting them. This is a similar case for most Asian countries such as the Philippines, Thailand, Vietnam, Singapore, etc.
</p><p>Positive self-perceptions of ageing are associated with better mental and physical health and well-being.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sabatini2019_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sabatini2019-237">[237]</a></sup> Positive <a href="/wiki/Self-rated_health" title="Self-rated health">self-perception of health</a> has been correlated with higher well-being and reduced mortality among the elderly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idler2003_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-Idler2003-238">[238]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deeg2003_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deeg2003-239">[239]</a></sup> Various reasons have been proposed for this association; people who are objectively healthy may naturally rate their health better as than that of their ill counterparts, though this link has been observed even in studies which have controlled for <a href="/wiki/Socioeconomic_status" title="Socioeconomic status">socioeconomic status</a>, psychological functioning and health status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benyamini2003_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-Benyamini2003-240">[240]</a></sup> This finding is generally stronger for men than women,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deeg2003_239-1"><a href="#cite_note-Deeg2003-239">[239]</a></sup> though this relationship is not universal across all studies and may only be true in some circumstances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Benyamini2003_240-1"><a href="#cite_note-Benyamini2003-240">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p>As people age, subjective health remains relatively stable, even though objective health worsens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kunz2000_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kunz2000-241">[241]</a></sup> In fact, perceived health improves with age when objective health is controlled in the equation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> This phenomenon is known as the "paradox of ageing". This may be a result of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_comparison" title="Social comparison">social comparison</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> for instance, the older people get, the more they may consider themselves in better health than their same-aged peers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup> Elderly people often associate their functional and physical decline with the normal ageing process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup>
</p><p>One way to help younger people experience what it feels like to be older is through an <a href="/wiki/Ageing_suit" title="Ageing suit">ageing suit</a>. There are several different kinds of suits including the GERT (named as a reference to <a href="/wiki/Gerontology" title="Gerontology">gerontology</a>), the R70i exoskeleton, and the AGNES (Age Gain Now Empathy Suit) suits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-247">[247]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-249">[249]</a></sup> These suits create the feelings of the effects of ageing by adding extra weight and increased pressure in certain points like the wrists, ankles and other joints. In addition, the various suits have different ways to impair vision and hearing to simulate the loss of these senses. To create the loss of feeling in hands that the elderly experience, special gloves are a part of the uniforms.
</p><p>Use of these suits may help to increase the amount of empathy felt for the elderly and could be considered particularly useful for those who are either learning about ageing, or those who work with the elderly, such as nurses or care center staff.
</p><p>Empathy is another field that could benefit from the empathy these suits may cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_247-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-247">[247]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_249-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-249">[249]</a></sup> When designers understand what it feels like to have the impairments of old age, they can better design buildings, packaging, or even tools to help with the simple day-to-day tasks that are more difficult with less dexterity. Designing with the elderly in mind may help to reduce the negative feelings that are associated with the loss of abilities that the elderly face.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Successful_ageing">Successful ageing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Successful ageing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The concept of <i>successful ageing</i> can be traced back to the 1950s and was popularized in the 1980s. Traditional definitions of successful ageing have emphasized absence of physical and cognitive disabilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> In their 1987 article, Rowe and Kahn characterized successful ageing as involving three components: a) freedom from disease and disability, b) high cognitive and physical functioning, and c) social and productive engagement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Human_aging:_Usual_and_successful_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Human_aging:_Usual_and_successful-251">[251]</a></sup> The study cited previous was also done back in 1987 and therefore, these factors associated with successful aging have probably been changed. With the current knowledge, scientists started to focus on learning about the effect spirituality in successful aging. There are some differences in cultures which of these components are the most important. Most often across cultures social engagement was the most highly rated but depending on the culture the definition of successful ageing changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_references">Cultural references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ageing&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Cultural references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ancient Greek dramatist <a href="/wiki/Euripides" title="Euripides">Euripides</a> (5th century BC) describes the multiple-headed mythological monster <a href="/wiki/Lernaean_Hydra" title="Lernaean Hydra">Hydra</a> as having a regenerative capacity which makes it immortal, which is the historical background to the name of the biological genus <a href="/wiki/Hydra_(genus)" title="Hydra (genus)">Hydra</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Job" title="Book of Job">Book of Job</a> (c. 6th century BC) describes human lifespan as inherently limited and makes a comparison with the innate immortality that a felled tree may have when undergoing vegetative regeneration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup>
</p>
